<p><b>Fotbal Club Universitatea Cluj</b> (<small>Romanian pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Romanian" title="Help:IPA for Romanian">[universiˈtate̯a kluʒ]</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romanian</a> professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> club from <a href="/wiki/Cluj-Napoca" title="Cluj-Napoca">Cluj-Napoca</a>, founded in 1919 by <a href="/wiki/Iuliu_Ha%C8%9Bieganu" title="Iuliu Hațieganu">Iuliu Hațieganu</a>. The team plays in Romania's fourth league, <a href="/wiki/Liga_IV" title="Liga IV">Liga IV</a>. Universitatea Cluj traditionally plays in white and black clothing, although variations of red, maroon and gold have been used—especially for away kits. U Cluj played for 89 years at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ion_Moina_Stadium" title="Ion Moina Stadium">Ion Moina Stadium</a>, and then moved into the new venue <a href="/wiki/Cluj_Arena" title="Cluj Arena">Cluj Arena</a>, built on the site of the old stadium.</p>
<p>U Cluj are nicknamed <i>Șepcile roșii</i> ("The Red Caps") after the red berets worn by students from the <a href="/wiki/Iuliu_Ha%C8%9Bieganu_University_of_Medicine_and_Pharmacy" title="Iuliu Hațieganu University of Medicine and Pharmacy">University of Medicine</a> in Cluj. They are traditionally considered to be the most important football club in <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a>, although their status has recently been threatened by the success of their city rivals <a href="/wiki/CFR_Cluj" title="CFR Cluj">CFR Cluj</a>.</p>
<p>The club has spent most of its history in the first league but have never become national champions. They have played in four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romanian_Cup" title="Romanian Cup">Romanian Cup</a> finals—each time under a different name—and won the trophy in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1964-65_Cupa_Rom%C3%A2niei" title="1964-65 Cupa României">1964–65 season</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Universitatea_Cluj&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <i>Universitatea</i> sports club of Cluj was founded in September 1919 by the "<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sports_Society_of_University_Students&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sports Society of University Students (page does not exist)">Sports Society of University Students</a>" (<a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>: <span lang="ro" xml:lang="ro"><i>Societatea Sportivă a Studenților Universitari</i></span>—abbreviated to "U"). Its first chairman was Professor Iuliu Hațieganu, a physician and politician. In the early years of its existence "U" Cluj played in local competitions; at the time there was no national football championship in Romania. The team played against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinezul" title="Chinezul">Chinezul Timișoara</a> in the 1923 final of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mara_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mara Cup (page does not exist)">Mara Cup</a>, losing 0–2. "U" played in the Romanian national football championship <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Divizia_A" title="Divizia A">Divizia A</a> from 1932. In their <a href="/wiki/1932%E2%80%9333_Divizia_A" title="1932–33 Divizia A">first season</a> "U" finished first in its group and played the championship final against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ripensia_Timi%C8%99oara" title="Ripensia Timișoara">Ripensia Timișoara</a> (0–0 and 3–5).</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1934---ripensia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="564" data-file-width="800" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/1934---ripensia.jpg/200px-1934---ripensia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/1934---ripensia.jpg/300px-1934---ripensia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/1934---ripensia.jpg/400px-1934---ripensia.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1934---ripensia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ripensia Timișoara winning the <a href="/wiki/1933%E2%80%9334_Cupa_Rom%C3%A2niei" title="1933–34 Cupa României">1933–34 Romanian Cup</a> against "U"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/1933%E2%80%9334_Cupa_Rom%C3%A2niei" title="1933–34 Cupa României">first season of the Romanian Cup</a>, in 1933–34, "U" reached the final, losing against Ripensia Timișoara (0–5). In 1940, "U" moved from Cluj to <a href="/wiki/Sibiu" title="Sibiu">Sibiu</a> as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Vienna_Award" title="Second Vienna Award">Second Vienna Award</a>, when the northern part of Transylvania was ceded to <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>. In 1942, "U" played in the <a href="/wiki/1942%E2%80%9343_Cupa_Rom%C3%A2niei" title="1942–43 Cupa României">final of the Romanian Cup</a> for a second time and lost against <a href="/wiki/FC_Rapid_Bucure%C8%99ti" title="FC Rapid București">Rapid București</a> (1–7). In 1945, after the end of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Treaties,_1947" title="Paris Peace Treaties, 1947">return of the northern part of Transylvania</a> to Romania, "U" returned to its home in Cluj.</p>
<p>In 1946, the name of the club was changed to <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C8%98tiin%C8%9Ba_Cluj" title="Știința Cluj">Știința Cluj</a></i> (English: Science Cluj). In 1949, the team reached the <a href="/wiki/1948%E2%80%9349_Cupa_Rom%C3%A2niei" title="1948–49 Cupa României">final of the Romanian Cup</a> for the third time, but it was beaten by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CSCA_Bucure%C8%99ti" title="CSCA București">CSCA București</a>—now called <a href="/wiki/FC_Steaua_Bucure%C8%99ti" title="FC Steaua București">Steaua București</a> (1–2).</p>
<p>At the end of the 1950s and the beginning of the 1960s, the manager of Știința Cluj was <a href="/wiki/%C8%98tefan_Kov%C3%A1cs" title="Ștefan Kovács">Ștefan Kovács</a>—a famous Romanian coach who later became the manager of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ajax_Amsterdam" title="Ajax Amsterdam">Ajax Amsterdam</a>. In <a href="/wiki/1964%E2%80%9365_Cupa_Rom%C3%A2niei" title="1964–65 Cupa României">1964–65</a>, <i>Știința Cluj</i> won the Romanian Cup; this remained the greatest performance of the club for many years.</p>
<p>In 1966, the name of the team was changed back to "Universitatea". At the end of the <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_Divizia_A" title="1971–72 Divizia A">1971–1972 season</a>, "U" was in the best position in the Romanian Championship Divizia A after the Second World War; it finished third in the league table, with the same number of points as the second placed team <a href="/wiki/FC_UTA_Arad" title="FC UTA Arad">UTA Arad</a>. In 1998, "U" reached the final of <a href="/wiki/Cupa_Ligii" title="Cupa Ligii">Cupa Ligii</a> but lost to <a href="/wiki/FCM_Bac%C4%83u" title="FCM Bacău">FCM Bacău</a>. <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_Divizia_A" title="1998–99 Divizia A">In 1999</a>, "U" was relegated into the second Romanian division, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Divizia_B" title="Divizia B">Divizia B</a> and <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Divizia_B" title="1999–2000 Divizia B">in 2000</a> it was relegated for the first time in its history into the third division, <a href="/wiki/Liga_III" title="Liga III">Divizia C</a>. It played one season in the third division, and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=2000%E2%80%9301_Divizia_C&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="2000–01 Divizia C (page does not exist)">in 2001</a> it was promoted back to Divizia B. The manager of the team at the time was the ex-Romanian international, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ioan_Ovidiu_Sab%C4%83u" title="Ioan Ovidiu Sabău">Ioan Ovidiu Sabău</a>—who started playing football in the 1980s at "U" Cluj.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Divizia_B" title="2005–06 Divizia B">2005–06 Divizia B season</a>, the new objective became promotion to the first league. Under coach <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Leo_Grozavu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Leo Grozavu (page does not exist)">Leo Grozavu</a>, who often played highly defensive football,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> the team made many nil draws and the team lost second place (promotion play-off) by a point, though in the last match days they won 4–0 with the first place and the third, and 3–2 (after leading 3–0) with the 2nd place.</p>
<p>In the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Liga_II" title="2006–07 Liga II">2006–07 Liga II season</a> (Divizia B was renamed to Liga II in this season), a new manager, <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Falub" title="Adrian Falub">Adrian Falub</a>—who had never coached before but had played over 220 matches for "U" Cluj in the first league—was hired. Under his lead, the team had a poor early season and only reached 8th position. Yet, the moment passed and the team reached 1st position, often separated by over 6 points from the next position. On 19 May 2007, virtual promotion was achieved after a 0–0 draw against second place contender <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dacia_Mioveni" title="Dacia Mioveni">Dacia Mioveni</a>. Three weeks before the final match day, "U" ended its 8-year spell in the lower divisions, <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Liga_I" title="2007–08 Liga I">returning to the first league</a> for the 52nd season in its history.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium">Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Universitatea_Cluj&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stadionul_Ion_Moina.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="193" data-file-width="300" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Stadionul_Ion_Moina.JPG/220px-Stadionul_Ion_Moina.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4f/Stadionul_Ion_Moina.JPG 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stadionul_Ion_Moina.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Stadionul_Ion_Moina_(1911)" title="Stadionul Ion Moina (1911)">old Ion Moina Stadium</a> (1911–2008), the former home ground of U Cluj</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cluj-Arena.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="640" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Cluj-Arena.jpg/220px-Cluj-Arena.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Cluj-Arena.jpg/330px-Cluj-Arena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Cluj-Arena.jpg/440px-Cluj-Arena.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cluj-Arena.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Cluj_Arena" title="Cluj Arena">Cluj Arena</a>, the current home ground of U Cluj</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ion_Moina_Stadium" title="Ion Moina Stadium">Ion Moina Stadium</a>, the first football and athletics stadium in <a href="/wiki/Cluj-Napoca" title="Cluj-Napoca">Cluj-Napoca</a>, was built between 1908 and 1911 and had a capacity of 1,500. The official inauguration in 1911 was a game between a Cluj team and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(football_team)" title="Galatasaray S.K. (football team)">Galatasaray Istanbul</a>. It was the first game in Europe for Galatasaray; the Cluj team won 8–1. In 1961, new U-shaped stands were built and the capacity of the stadium became 28,000. In 2000, most of the stands were declared structurally unsafe for hosting supporters and were closed, leaving the stadium with a capacity of 12–13,000. In late 2008, the old "Ion Moina" Stadium was demolished, and building works begun for the <a href="/wiki/Cluj_Arena" title="Cluj Arena">Cluj Arena</a>. The last official game at the old stadium was played on 22 November 2008; Universitatea drew 0–0 in <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Liga_II" title="2008–09 Liga II">their Liga II game</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mure%C8%99ul_Deva" title="Mureșul Deva">Mureșul Deva</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the construction works for the new stadium, Universitatea played its home games in the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Liga_II" title="2008–09 Liga II">2008–09</a> and <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Liga_II" title="2009–10 Liga II">2009–10</a> Liga II seasons at the <a href="/wiki/Stadionul_Clujana" title="Stadionul Clujana">Clujana Stadium</a> and its home games in the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Liga_I" title="2010–11 Liga I">2010–11 Liga I</a> season at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stadionul_Victoria-Cetate" title="Stadionul Victoria-Cetate">Cetate Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Alba_Iulia" title="Alba Iulia">Alba Iulia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stadionul_Gloria" title="Stadionul Gloria">Gloria Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bistri%C8%9Ba" title="Bistrița">Bistrița</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stadionul_Gaz_Metan" title="Stadionul Gaz Metan">Gaz Metan Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Media%C8%99" title="Mediaș">Mediaș</a>.</p>
<p>On 11 October 2011, the first match at the new Cluj Arena stadium—a friendly between Universitatea and the <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> team <a href="/wiki/FC_Kuban_Krasnodar" title="FC Kuban Krasnodar">Kuban Krasnodar</a>—was played; Kuban won 4–0. On 16 October 2011, the first official match at the new stadium was played; Universitatea won the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Liga_I" title="2011–12 Liga I">Liga I game</a> against <a href="/wiki/FC_Bra%C8%99ov" title="FC Brașov">FC Brașov</a> 1–0.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Supporters">Supporters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Universitatea_Cluj&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Supporters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Suporteri_U_CLUJ.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2255" data-file-width="3455" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Suporteri_U_CLUJ.jpg/220px-Suporteri_U_CLUJ.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Suporteri_U_CLUJ.jpg/330px-Suporteri_U_CLUJ.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Suporteri_U_CLUJ.jpg/440px-Suporteri_U_CLUJ.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Suporteri_U_CLUJ.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
”U” Cluj supporters during a First Division game</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>“U” has many supporters in <a href="/wiki/Cluj-Napoca" title="Cluj-Napoca">Cluj-Napoca</a>, but also in some other parts of Romania—especially in Transylvania. One of the reasons for the team’s popularity is that Cluj-Napoca has some of Romania's most important universities—including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Babes-Bolyai_University" title="Babes-Bolyai University">Babes-Bolyai University</a>, the largest in the country with more than 45,000 students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>The ultras groups of "U" Cluj are: VG (Vechia Guardia), Fazione Accademica, UCG (Ultra Curva Groapa), Ultras 19, Fanatics, Boys, Battaglione Gheorgheni, F.O.R.T. and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Universitatea_Cluj&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uclujsuporteri.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="864" data-file-width="1152" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Uclujsuporteri.jpg/220px-Uclujsuporteri.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Uclujsuporteri.jpg/330px-Uclujsuporteri.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Uclujsuporteri.jpg/440px-Uclujsuporteri.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Uclujsuporteri.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
”U” Cluj supporters during a Second Division game</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Universitatea have a rivalry with local city team <a href="/wiki/CFR_Cluj" title="CFR Cluj">CFR Cluj</a>. The animosity between the teams is one of the oldest in Romanian football.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-voceatransilvaniei.ro_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-voceatransilvaniei.ro-5">[5]</a></sup> The first incidents between fans of the two sides occurred in the 1920s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-voceatransilvaniei.ro_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-voceatransilvaniei.ro-5">[5]</a></sup> A particularly violent episode took place during a derby played in 1924, when the stadium had to be evacuated because of a large-scale fight between supporters. Universitatea won the match 2–1. Other episodes of this rivalry are: in 2005, upset by the fact that Universitatea was relegated to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Divizia_C" title="Divizia C">Divizia C</a>, "U" fans injured CFR players at the Sport Hotel in <a href="/wiki/Cluj-Napoca" title="Cluj-Napoca">Cluj-Napoca</a>; in 2008, following a derby, CFR won and obtained its first league title and Universitatea relegated in <a href="/wiki/Liga_II" title="Liga II">Liga II</a>, but this match was preceded by a corruption scandal, because <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steaua_Bucure%C8%99ti" title="Steaua București">Steaua București</a>'s owner, <a href="/wiki/Gigi_Becali" title="Gigi Becali">Gigi Becali</a>, offered "U" staff one million euros for defeating CFR.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Junior_Teams">Junior Teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Universitatea_Cluj&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Junior Teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The “U” Cluj Under 21 and Junior teams have always ranked among the best in the country and have won several National Championship titles:</p>
<ul>
<li>The Under-21s were Romanian champions 3 times in: 1962–63, 1970–71, 1971–72</li>
<li>The Under-21s were Romanian champions 8 times in: 1955, 1956, 1964–65, 1966–67, 1968–69, 1971–72, 1973–74, 2000–01</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Key">Key</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Universitatea_Cluj&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Key">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div>
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 33.33%;text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">
<ul>
<li>Pos = Final position</li>
<li>P = Played</li>
<li>W = Games won</li>
<li>D = Games drawn</li>
<li>L = Games lost</li>
<li>GF = Goals For</li>
<li>GA = Goals Against</li>
<li>Pts = Points</li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="width: 33.33%;text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">
<ul>
<li>Div A / L1 = <a href="/wiki/Liga_I" title="Liga I">Liga I</a></li>
<li>Div B / L2 = <a href="/wiki/Liga_II" title="Liga II">Liga II</a></li>
<li>Div C / L3 = <a href="/wiki/Liga_III" title="Liga III">Liga III</a></li>
<li>L4 = <a href="/wiki/Liga_IV" title="Liga IV">Liga IV</a></li>
<li>p = Preliminary Round</li>
<li>1R = Round 1</li>
<li>2R = Round 2</li>
<li>3R = Round 3</li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="width: 33.33%;text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">
<ul>
<li>4R = Round 4</li>
<li>5R = Round 5</li>
<li>GS = Group stage</li>
<li>R32 = Round of 32</li>
<li>QF = Quarter-finals</li>
<li>R16 = Round of 16</li>
<li>SF = Semi-finals</li>
<li>F = Final</li>
</ul>
</td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_former_players">Notable former players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Universitatea_Cluj&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Notable former players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The footballers enlisted below have had international cap(s) for their respective countries at junior and/or senior level. Players whose name is listed in <b>bold</b> represented their countries at junior and/or senior level on through the time's passing. Additionally, these players have also had a significant number of caps and goals accumulated throughout a certain number of seasons for the club itself as well.</p>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For a list of all former and current Universitatea Cluj players with a Wikipedia article, see <a href="/wiki/Category:FC_Universitatea_Cluj_players" title="Category:FC Universitatea Cluj players">Category:FC Universitatea Cluj players</a>.</div>
